# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of the JVM bytecode interpreter main dispatch loop implementation in OpenJDK. The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json`.

## Summary

I've identified **45 C++ source files** that implement the JVM bytecode interpreter in openjdk/jdk:

### Key Components:

1. **Bytecode Dispatch Table** - The `DispatchTable` class in `templateInterpreter.cpp/hpp` that contains indexed arrays of bytecode handler addresses organized by TosState (Top Of Stack state) and bytecode type.

2. **Interpreter Template Generation** - The `TemplateInterpreterGenerator` class that generates pre-compiled bytecode handlers and populates dispatch tables. This includes architecture-specific generators for x86, ARM, AArch64, PowerPC, RISC-V, and S390.

3. **Method Entry Point Setup** - The `generate_method_entry()` function that creates entry points for different method kinds (abstract, empty, synchronized, native, etc.).

4. **Bytecode Implementations** - The `TemplateTable` class with architecture-specific template implementations for each Java bytecode instruction.

5. **Alternative Zero Interpreter** - For platforms without JIT, the `BytecodeInterpreter::run()` and `ZeroInterpreter::main_loop()` provide an alternative dispatch mechanism using a switch statement.

The dispatch mechanism works by using pre-generated dispatch tables to jump directly to bytecode handler code, with safepoint variants for GC coordination. All files are included in the answer.json output file.

\"text\": \"The JVM bytecode interpreter main dispatch loop in OpenJDK is implemented across several key C++ source files. The TemplateInterpreter architecture uses a dispatch table approach where bytecode handlers are pre-generated and organized in tables indexed by bytecode type and stack state (TosState - Top Of Stack state).\\n\\n**Core Dispatch Table Implementation:**\\nThe main dispatch table is defined in src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.hpp as the `DispatchTable` class. This class contains three dispatch tables: _active_table (currently active), _normal_table (normal dispatch), and _safept_table (safepoint variant). The dispatch tables are arrays of addresses indexed by both TosState and bytecode value. The DispatchTable class is initialized and used in src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.cpp.\\n\\n**Interpreter Template Generation:**\\nThe src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreterGenerator.cpp is the core file that generates the entire interpreter. The `TemplateInterpreterGenerator` class uses the `generate_all()` method to:\\n1. Generate the slow signature handler\\n2. Generate error exits\\n3. Generate return entry points\\n4. Generate method entries for various method kinds (zerolocals, synchronized, abstract, native, math intrinsics, etc.)\\n5. Populate the dispatch tables with bytecode handler addresses\\n\\nMethod entry points are set up via `TemplateInterpreterGenerator::generate_method_entry()` which creates entry points for different method kinds (abstract, empty, getter, setter, zerolocals, etc.).\\n\\n**Platform-Specific Code Generation:**\\nEach CPU architecture (x86, ARM, AArch64, PowerPC, RISC-V, S390) has its own implementation files:\\n- `templateInterpreterGenerator_*.cpp` - Generates architecture-specific interpreter code\\n- `templateTable_*.cpp` - Contains architecture-specific bytecode implementations\\n- `interp_masm_*.cpp` - Interpreter macro assembler with dispatch mechanisms\\n- `abstractInterpreter_*.cpp` - Framework calculations specific to the architecture\\n\\n**Bytecode Dispatch Table:**\\nThe src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateTable.cpp and .hpp files define the `TemplateTable` class which holds template entries for each bytecode. These templates are pre-generated code snippets that implement each bytecode instruction.\\n\\n**Zero Interpreter (Alternative Implementation):**\\nFor platforms without JIT compilation support, the Zero interpreter provides an alternative main dispatch loop:\\n- src/hotspot/share/interpreter/zero/bytecodeInterpreter.cpp implements the main bytecode interpretation loop via `BytecodeInterpreter::run()` template method\\n- src/hotspot/cpu/zero/zeroInterpreter_zero.cpp implements the `ZeroInterpreter::main_loop()` which invokes the bytecode interpreter\\n- The Zero interpreter dispatches bytecodes via a switch statement over bytecode types rather than using pre-generated dispatch tables\\n\\n**Execution Flow:**\\nWhen a method is invoked, the entry point table (Interpreter::_entry_table) directs execution to the appropriate method entry point based on the method kind. The dispatch mechanism then uses the dispatch table (Interpreter::dispatch_table()) to jump to the appropriate bytecode handler, which after execution loads the next bytecode and repeats the cycle. The safepoint table (Interpreter::_safept_table) provides alternative safepoint-aware dispatch entries.\\n\\nAll these components work together to form the complete JVM bytecode interpretation infrastructure, allowing the HotSpot VM to execute Java bytecode either through pre-compiled template-based dispatch (TemplateInterpreter) or through the Zero interpreter's main loop.\"\n}\n",

The TemplateInterpreter architecture uses a dispatch table approach where bytecode handlers are pre-generated and organized in tables indexed by bytecode type and stack state (TosState - Top Of Stack state).\\n\\n**Core Dispatch Table Implementation:**\\nThe main dispatch table is defined in src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.hpp as the `DispatchTable` class. This class contains three dispatch tables: _active_table (currently active), _normal_table (normal dispatch), and _safept_table (safepoint variant). The dispatch tables are arrays of addresses indexed by both TosState and bytecode value. The DispatchTable class is initialized and used in src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreter.cpp.\\n\\n**Interpreter Template Generation:**\\nThe src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateInterpreterGenerator.cpp is the core file that generates the entire interpreter. The `TemplateInterpreterGenerator` class uses the `generate_all()` method to:\\n1. Generate the slow signature handler\\n2. Generate error exits\\n3. Generate return entry points\\n4. Generate method entries for various method kinds (zerolocals, synchronized, abstract, native, math intrinsics, etc.)\\n5. Populate the dispatch tables with bytecode handler addresses\\n\\nMethod entry points are set up via `TemplateInterpreterGenerator::generate_method_entry()` which creates entry points for different method kinds (abstract, empty, getter, setter, zerolocals, etc.).\\n\\n**Platform-Specific Code Generation:**\\nEach CPU architecture (x86, ARM, AArch64, PowerPC, RISC-V, S390) has its own implementation files:\\n- `templateInterpreterGenerator_*.cpp` - Generates architecture-specific interpreter code\\n- `templateTable_*.cpp` - Contains architecture-specific bytecode implementations\\n- `interp_masm_*.cpp` - Interpreter macro assembler with dispatch mechanisms\\n- `abstractInterpreter_*.cpp` - Framework calculations specific to the architecture\\n\\n**Bytecode Dispatch Table:**\\nThe src/hotspot/share/interpreter/templateTable.cpp and .hpp files define the `TemplateTable` class which holds template entries for each bytecode. These templates are pre-generated code snippets that implement each bytecode instruction.\\n\\n**Zero Interpreter (Alternative Implementation):**\\nFor platforms without JIT compilation support, the Zero interpreter provides an alternative main dispatch loop:\\n- src/hotspot/share/interpreter/zero/bytecodeInterpreter.cpp implements the main bytecode interpretation loop via `BytecodeInterpreter::run()` template method\\n- src/hotspot/cpu/zero/zeroInterpreter_zero.cpp implements the `ZeroInterpreter::main_loop()` which invokes the bytecode interpreter\\n- The Zero interpreter dispatches bytecodes via a switch statement over bytecode types rather than using pre-generated dispatch tables\\n\\n**Execution Flow:**\\nWhen a method is invoked, the entry point table (Interpreter::_entry_table) directs execution to the appropriate method entry point based on the method kind. The dispatch mechanism then uses the dispatch table (Interpreter::dispatch_table()) to jump to the appropriate bytecode handler, which after execution loads the next bytecode and repeats the cycle. The safepoint table (Interpreter::_safept_table) provides alternative safepoint-aware dispatch entries.\\n\\nAll these components work together to form the complete JVM bytecode interpretation infrastructure, allowing the HotSpot VM to execute Java bytecode either through pre-compiled template-based dispatch (TemplateInterpreter) or through the Zero interpreter's main loop.\"\n}\n",
